        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  For sodium (Na)-rechargeable batteries to compete, and go beyond the currently prevailing Li-ion technologies, mastering the chem. and accompanying phenomena is of supreme importance.  Among the crucial components of the battery system, the electrolyte, which bridges the highly polarized pos. and neg. electrode materials, is arguably the most crit. and indispensable of all.  The electrolyte dictates the interfacial chem. of the battery and the overall performance, having an influence over the practical capacity, rate capability (power), chem./thermal stress (safety), and lifetime.  In-depth knowledge of electrolyte properties provides invaluable information to improve the design, assembly, and operation of the battery.  Thus, the full-scale appraisal of both tailored electrolytes and the concomitant interphases generated at the electrodes need to be prioritized.  The deployment of large-format Na-based rechargeable batteries also necessitates systematic evaluation and detailed appraisal of the safety-related hazards of Na-based batteries.  Hence, this review presents a comprehensive account of the progress, status, and prospect of various Na+-ion electrolytes, including solvents, salts and additives, their interphases and potential hazards.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGofTJQHxRfLdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5rGvXSQHMlg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXmsVWrur8%253D&amp;md5=da4e158754e397377d3896e6a2bc627d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600943"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, Kim</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Lee</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, Yoon</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress in Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. L.; Gao, Peiyuan; Xu, Yaobin; Xiao, Biwei; Engelhard, Mark H.; Cao, Xia; Vo, Thanh D.; Hu, Jiangtao; Zhong, Lirong; Matthews, Bethany E.; Yi, Ran; Wang, Chongmin; Li, Xiaolin; Liu, Jun; Zhang, Ji-Guang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Portfolio</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) have attracted worldwide attention for next-generation energy storage systems.  However, the severe instability of the solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed during repeated cycling hinders the development of NIBs.  In particular, the SEI dissoln. in NIBs with a high-voltage cathode is more severe than in the case of Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and leads to continuous side reactions, electrolyte depletion and irreversible capacity loss, making NIBs less stable than LIBs.  Here we report a rational electrolyte design to suppress the SEI dissoln. and enhance NIB performance.  Our electrolyte lowers the solvation ability for SEI components and facilitates the formation of insol. SEI components, which minimizes the SEI dissoln.  In addn. to the stable SEI on a hard carbon (HC) anode, we also show a stable interphase formation on a NaNi0.68Mn0.22Co0.1O2 (NaNMC) cathode.  Our HC||NaNMC full cell with this electrolyte demonstrates &gt;90% capacity retention after 300 cycles when charged to 4.2 V.  This study enables high-voltage NIBs with long cycling performance and provides a guiding principle in electrolyte design for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp6-mgtLx7nR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5rGvXSQHMlg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhvVCntbbJ&amp;md5=27df3174814e23e6530bb6a56e2037b4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/inf2.12023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Zeheng</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent research progresses in ether- and ester-based electrolytes for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>InfoMater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">376</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">389</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Marriage of an Ether-Based Electrolyte with Hard Carbon Anodes Creates Superior Sodium-Ion Batteries with High Mass Loading</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Yongwu; Bai, Panxing; Gao, Shuyan; Xu, Yunhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Inferior rate performance, insufficient cycle life, and low mass loading have restricted the practical application of hard C (HC) anodes in Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Here, a compatible strategy is developed by matching HC anodes with an ether-based electrolyte.  A systematic study reveals that good compatibility of the electrode-electrolyte systems forms thinner but a more sustainable solid-electrolyte interphase and delivers a higher ionic cond. and Na+ ion diffusion coeff. than the commonly used ester-based electrolytes.  Therefore, an excellent electrochem. performance is demonstrated with a long cycle life (∼196 mAh/g and 90% capacity retention after 2000 cycles at 1 A/g), a super rate capability (∼51% capacity retention at 10 A/g) at a mass loading of 1.5 mg/cm2, and a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 85.9%.  A high reversible areal capacity of 4.3 mAh/cm2 can be achieved at an ultrahigh mass loading of 17 mg/cm2, superior to all reported HC anodes.  Our findings not only shed light on the design of high-performance battery systems but also promise a com. transformation from the lab. test to mass prodn. of NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrBl0ltiwR75bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5rGvXSQHMlg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitFWmu7rI&amp;md5=840c025e787c6f6eaeda77e95bf38325</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2021.07.021"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hirsh, Sayahpour</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Li</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Zhao</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Role of electrolyte in stabilizing hard carbon as an anode for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries with long cycle life</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>42</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">78</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">87</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although being the std. anode material in Li-ion batteries (LIBs), graphite so far is considered to fail application in Na-ion batteries (NIBs) because the Na-C system lacks suitable binary intercalation compds.  This limitation can be circumvented by using co-intercalation phenomena in a diglyme-based electrolyte.  The resulting compd. is a stage-I ternary intercalation compd. with an estd. stoichiometry of Na(diglyme)2C20.  Highlights of the electrode reaction are its high energy efficiency, the small irreversible loss during the 1st cycle, and a superior cycle life with capacities close to 100 mA-h g-1 for 1000 cycles and coulomb efficiencies &gt;99.87%.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced rate and cyclability of a porous Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode using dimethyl ether as the electrolyte for application in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sadan, Milan K.; Kim, Huihun; Kim, Changhyeon; Cha, Seung Hwan; Cho, Kwon-Koo; Kim, Ki-Won; Ahn, Jou-Hyeon; Ahn, Hyo-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium vanadium phosphate (NVP) is a potential cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, but its rate capability requires improvement.  Herein, the electrode-electrolyte interface is modified using di-Me ether (DME) electrolyte, such that the porous NVP cathode leads to ultrafast kinetics and ultra-long cycle life in comparison to those obsd. using conventional ethylene carbonate/propylene carbonate electrolytes.  The rate capability and cycle life are the highest reported to date.  The Na/NVP half-cell with DME affords good capacity (44 mA h g-1 at 100 A g-1; 854C) and stable ultra-long cycle life for 95 000 cycles with a negligible degrdn. rate (5.8 x 10-5 % per cycle at 50 A g-1, i.e., 1.05 Na+ reversibly reacts with NVP within 4.5 s).  The NVP full cell coupled with a Sn anode delivers a reversible capacity of 70 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1 for 5000 cycles with 100% coulombic efficiency.  After 5000 cycles, the energy d. is 217 W h kg-1 and the power d. is 30 985 W kg-1 (based on NVP mass).  The DME electrolyte effectively modifies the interface for fast kinetics both as a half-cell and a full cell.  This simple strategy can be extended to other battery systems to achieve fast kinetics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGolDhZF6d5bvbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liH44u0cLxXzg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXptFGlsr8%253D&amp;md5=1dd6ea1af2d9e7c3106080347b39747b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.8b00360"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Westman, Dugas</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jankowski, Wieczorek</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gachot, Morcrette</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Irisarri, Ponrouch</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palacín, Tarascon</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Johansson</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Diglyme Based Electrolytes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are currently being considered for large-scale energy storage.  Optimization of SIB electrolytes is, however, still largely lacking.  Here the authors exhaustively evaluate NaPF6 in diglyme as an electrolyte of choice - both physicochem. properties and extensive electrochem. tests including half as well as full cells.  Fundamentally, the ionic cond. is quite comparable to carbonate based electrolytes and obeying the fractional Walden rule with viscosity.  Na metal to work well as a ref. electrode and the electrochem. stability, evaluated potentiostatically for various electrodes and corroborated by DFT calcns., to be satisfactory in the entire voltage range of 0-4.4 V were found.  Galvanostatic cycling at C/10 of half and full cells using Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) or Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) as cathodes and hard C (Hc) as anodes indicate rapid capacity fading in cells with Hc anodes, possibly originating in a lack of a stable SEI or by trapping of Na.  Aiming to understand this capacity fade further, the authors conducted a GC/MS anal. to det. electrolyte redn. products and to propose redn. pathways, concluding that oligomer and/or alkoxide formation is possible.  Overall, the promising results should warrant further studies of diglyme based electrolytes for modern SIB development, albeit avoiding Hc anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFiF2ivdKMibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwc3DlE1W3xA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXpsl2gu7Y%253D&amp;md5=869d3cbc4f84288127bda52c4a990590</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501785"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, Kretschmer</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improved Electrochemical Performance of Na-Ion Batteries in Ether-Based Electrolytes: A Case Study of ZnS Nanospheres</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultralong Cycle Life Organic Cathode Enabled by Ether-Based Electrolytes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yuqing; Bai, Panxing; Li, Benfang; Zhao, Chen; Chen, Zifeng; Li, Mengjie; Su, Hai; Yang, Jixing; Xu, Yunhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. cathode materials have gained substantial attention in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of their low cost, structure versatility, and environmental friendliness.  Nevertheless, the use of org. materials is plagued by the unsatisfactory cycling performance caused by dissoln. of org. electrode materials, use of inappropriate electrolytes, and/or poor interfacial compatibility.  In this work, an ultralong cycle life of SIBs through coupling an insol. org. cathode, N, N'-bis(glycinyl) naphthalene diimide, with ether-based electrolytes, is realized.  A thin and stable inorg.-rich solid electrolyte interphase is constructed through a prior redn. of salt in the org. solvents in the ether-based electrolytes, promising fast charge transfer kinetics and stable cycling performance of org. electrodes in SIBs.  A superb long cycle life of 70 000 cycles at 10C is demonstrated, which is a new record for org. cathode materials in SIBs.  The findings highlight the key role of electrolytes and electrolyte/electrode interfaces in furthering the practical prospects of org. electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGprj8hWsyflNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwc3DlE1W3xA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhvFSqtLzE&amp;md5=05db70d8bd9afe7e2892659e6acf41be</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201805479"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Shi</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, Liang</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Safety Nonaqueous Electrolytes and Interphases for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>15</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">14</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e1805479</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Non-aqueous electrolytes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ponrouch, A.; Monti, D.; Boschin, A.; Steen, B.; Johansson, P.; Palacin, M. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22-42</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The 1st review of the various electrolytes currently used and developed for Na-ion batteries (SIBs), both in terms of materials and concepts, is presented.  In contrast to the Li-ion battery (LIB), which is a mature technol. for which a more or less unanimously accepted std. electrolyte exists: 1 M LiPF6 in EC/DMC, the electrolyte of choice for SIBs has not yet fully conformed to a std.  This is true for both materials: salts, solvents, or additives, and concept, using the main track of org. solvents or aiming for other concepts.  SIB research currently prospers, benefitting from using know-how gained from 30 years of LIB R and D.  Here the currently employed electrolytes are emphasized and their effects on practical SIB performance are outlined, scrutinizing the rationale for specific choices made, salts, solvents, additives, concns., etc. for each specific cell set-up and usage conditions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpb_d9E3Qe0wLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwc3DlE1W3xA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhslOjtLfI&amp;md5=b99d9ac3e00e101e25ffc33ee1bef953</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.10.006"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Han</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Xiong</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Sun</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solid electrolyte interphase manipulation towards highly stable hard carbon anodes for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">324</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">333</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interfacial engineering to achieve an energy density of over 200 Wh kg-1 in sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yuqi; Zhou, Quan; Weng, Suting; Ding, Feixiang; Qi, Xingguo; Lu, Jiaze; Li, Yu; Zhang, Xiao; Rong, Xiaohui; Lu, Yaxiang; Wang, Xuefeng; Xiao, Ruijuan; Li, Hong; Huang, Xuejie; Chen, Liquan; Hu, Yong-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">511-519</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-based batteries have attracted wide interests in the academic and industrial fields.  However, their energy d. is still lower than that of Li-based batteries.  Here we report an initial anode-free Na battery with an energy d. of over 200 Wh kg-1, which is even higher than that of the com. LiFePO4||graphite battery.  Through introducing graphitic carbon coating on the Al current collector and boron-contg. electrolytes in the battery, we show that uniform nucleation and robust interphases enable reversible and crack-free Na deposition.  Benefitting from the synergetic effects derived from the built cooperative interfaces, the cycling lifetime of the Na battery without applying addnl. pressure reaches 260 cycles, which is the longest life for large-size cells with zero excess Na.  The insights gained from the Na plating/stripping behavior and interfacial chem. in this work pave the way for further development of Na batteries with even higher performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqqWJKFVcBslLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgwc3DlE1W3xA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhvVCntbvL&amp;md5=b270eb982918f3375b0e3794577dc205</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202304162"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiaoli, Yi</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Uncovering the Redox Shuttle Degradation Mechanism of Ether Electrolytes in Sodium-Ion Batteries and its Inhibition Strategy</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e2304162</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Eu3+-doped pyridine functionalized YF3 microcrystals were synthesized at low temp. (70°) using a simple colloidal route.  The shape and phase of the YF3 microcrystals were tuned using different fluoride sources (e.g. NaF, NaBF4 and NH4F).  Cubic phase of the microcrystals with flower like morphol. was achieved with NaF as fluoride source, while use of NaBF4 and NH4F gave orthorhombic phase with bundle and rice flake like morphol., resp.         </div><div class="casAbstract">H-F exchange in the NaBH4-NaBF4 system is studied using a range of exptl. methods combined with DFT calcns. and a possible mechanism for the reactions is proposed.  F substitution is obsd. using in situ synchrotron radiation powder x-ray diffraction (SR-PXD) as a new Rock salt type compd. with idealized compn. NaBF2H2 in the temp. range T = 200 to 215°.  Combined use of solid-state 19F MASNMR, FTIR and DFT calcns. supports the formation of a BF2H2- complex ion, reproducing the observation of a 19F chem. shift at -144.2 ppm, which is different from that of NaBF4 at -159.2 ppm, along with the new absorption bands obsd. in the IR spectra. (300°) compared to NaBH4 (476°), as obsd. by TGA.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Low-Temperature Production of Glyceric Acid from Biomass-Based Sugar via the Cooperative Roles of MgO and NaBF4</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tian, Qing; Wang, Xiaoyan; Zhang, Wenyu; Liao, Shengqi; Hu, Changwei; Li, Jianmei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Industrial &amp; Engineering Chemistry Research</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Seeking new chemo-catalytic routes to produce glyceric acid using renewable biomass-based sugar as feedstock is of significance but remains a big challenge due to a quite low yield (&lt;5%).  Herein, we prep. an MgO catalyst with an oxygen vacancy and explore a simple but robust MgO-NaBF4 system, achieving the selective prodn. of glyceric acid from fructose with a high yield of 78.8% in an O2 atmosphere via chemo-catalysis at mild conditions (373 K), eliminating the use of strong inorg. alkalis and severe reaction conditions.  As far as we know, this has the highest value among the state-of-the-art chemo-catalytic strategies.  Evidenced by the isotope-probe expt. and theor. calcn., it was revealed that MgO and NaBF4 exhibited pronounced cooperative effects.  The hydroxyl group exposed on the MgO surface first facilitated the adsorption of fructose.  With the assistance of MgO, B(OH)4- from NaBF4 hydrolysis preferentially combined with β-D-fructofuranose, as evidenced by 11B and 13C NMR spectroscopy, due to its strong electron-withdrawing ability, producing a complex which could easily undergo ring-opening reaction with an attack of OH- derived from the alk. MgO.  More importantly, the oxygen vacancies on the MgO surface subsequently assisted the C3-C4 cleavage in fructose by MgO species to produce a glyceraldehyde intermediate and activated O2 to oxidize glyceraldehyde, yielding glyceric acid.  The conjunction of B(OH)4- with a glyceraldehyde intermediate or glyceric acid could also hinder its over-oxidn.  The insights in this work might provide new chemo-catalytic approaches for glyceric acid prodn. from renewable biomass.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqh5_JjyYHKUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOP1oxlenRBQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XivVWltbvI&amp;md5=b4e304727d0e7c96213c942fcf662a94</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1080/01932691.2021.1915155"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sultana, Habiba</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of ionic liquid on the micellization behavior of bile salts in aqueous medium</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of ionic liquid on the micellization behavior of bile salts in aqueous medium</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sultana, Habiba; Barai, Manas; Mandal, Manas Kumar; Manna, Emili; Maiti, Dilip Kumar; Dhara, Dibakar; Panda, Amiya Kumar</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Dispersion Science and Technology</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Interfacial and aggregation behavior of sodium cholate (NaC) and sodium deoxycholate (NaDC) in aq. ionic liq. (IL, 1-butyl-3-methylimidazolium tetrafluoroborate) medium were investigated.  Studies were also carried out in the presence of NaBF4.  Both IL and NaBF4 reduce the crit. micelle concn. (CMC) of bile salts, detd. by surface tension, conductance, and fluorescence spectroscopic techniques; effect of NaBF4 is more prominent than IL.  CMC of NaC was higher than NaDC because of its higher hydrophilicity.  IL, in addn. to its salt-like behavior, results in associative interaction with the bile salts.  Surface excess (Γmax), surface pressure at the CMC (πCMC) were evaluated from surface tension data. Γmax and πCMC values gradually decreased with increasing the IL and NaBF4 concn.  Neg. Gibbs free energy change for micellization (ΔG0mic) and interfacial adsorption (ΔG0ads) indicate spontaneity of micellization and interfacial adsorption, however to different magnitude.  Fraction of counter ion dissocn., evaluated from conductance data, systematically decreased with increasing IL and NaBF4 concn.  Aggregation no., detd. by fluorescence quenching method, increased with increasing IL and NaBF4 concn. that are in consonance with the size of the aggregates, detd. by dynamic light scattering study.  IL induced the formation of larger facial aggregates by bile salts; the effect was more imperative in case of NaDC than NaC.  In case of NaBF4 the opposite trend was recorded. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">10</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">11732</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">11740</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.0c18670</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D11732-11740%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26issue%3D10%26author%3DK.%2BDu%26author%3DA.%2BRudola%26author%3DP.%2BBalaya%26title%3DInvestigations%2Bof%2BThermal%2BStability%2Band%2BSolid%2BElectrolyte%2BInterphase%2Bon%2BNa%25282%2529Ti%25283%2529O%25287%2529%252FC%2Bas%2Ba%2BNon-carbonaceous%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BUsing%2BNon-flammable%2BEther-based%2BElectrolyte%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.0c18670&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c19126&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.0c18670&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigations of Thermal Stability and Solid Electrolyte Interphase on Na2Ti3O7/C as a Non-carbonaceous Anode Material for Sodium Storage Using Non-flammable Ether-based Electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Du, Kang; Rudola, Ashish; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11732-11740</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In order to become com. viable, sodium-ion batteries need to deliver long cycle life with good capacity and energy d. while still ensuring safety.  Electrolyte plays a key role forming solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layers at low potential, which affects the thermal stability and cycle life of the anode materials under consideration.  In this study, an ether-based non-flammable electrolyte, 1 M NaBF4 in tetraglyme, is tested for sodium storage using a non-carbonaceous anode material Na2Ti3O7/C, and the results are compared with those obtained with the popularly used carbonate-based electrolyte, 1 M NaClO4 in ethylene carbonate (EC) and propylene carbonate (PC) (vol./vol. = 1:1).  The Na2Ti3O7/C vs. Na cells using 1 M NaBF4 in tetraglyme show a much higher first cycle Coulombic efficiency (73%) than those using 1 M NaClO4 in EC/PC (33%).  Thermal stability studies using differential scanning calorimetry (DSC) conclusively show that Na2Ti3O7/C electrodes cycled with 1 M NaBF4 in tetraglyme are more thermally stable than the one cycled with 1 M NaClO4 in EC/PC.  Further investigations on the formation of SEI layers were performed using attenuated total reflection-Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, field-emission SEM, transmission electron microscopy, energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy, electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, and DSC studies.  These studies unambiguously demonstrate that the SEI formed on Na2Ti3O7/C using 1 M NaBF4 in tetraglyme is not only less resistive but also more stable than the SEI formed using 1 M NaClO4 in EC/PC.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpdlNs0OnsnmLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOP1oxlenRBQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXls1CrsL8%253D&amp;md5=8d4a98bd25e8fb1fbcb72ddb90b19b20</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2019.106635"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Yu</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Che, Haiying</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Xinrong</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, Yonghong</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lia, Linsen</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Zi-Feng</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Non-flammable organic electrolyte for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Electrochem.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stable Sodium Metal Batteries via Manipulation of Electrolyte Solvation Structure</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Shiyang; Chen, Yawei; Jie, Yulin; Lang, Shuangyan; Song, Junhua; Lei, Zhanwu; Wang, Shuai; Ren, Xiaodi; Wang, Dong; Li, Xiaolin; Cao, Ruiguo; Zhang, Genqiang; Jiao, Shuhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>

                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Low-solvation electrolytes for high-voltage sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Yan; Le, Phung M. L.; Gao, Peiyuan; Xu, Yaobin; Xiao, Biwei; Engelhard, Mark H.; Cao, Xia; Vo, Thanh D.; Hu, Jiangtao; Zhong, Lirong; Matthews, Bethany E.; Yi, Ran; Wang, Chongmin; Li, Xiaolin; Liu, Jun; Zhang, Ji-Guang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">718-725</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) have attracted worldwide attention for next-generation energy storage systems.  However, the severe instability of the solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed during repeated cycling hinders the development of NIBs.  In particular, the SEI dissoln. in NIBs with a high-voltage cathode is more severe than in the case of Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and leads to continuous side reactions, electrolyte depletion and irreversible capacity loss, making NIBs less stable than LIBs.  Here we report a rational electrolyte design to suppress the SEI dissoln. and enhance NIB performance.  Our electrolyte lowers the solvation ability for SEI components and facilitates the formation of insol. SEI components, which minimizes the SEI dissoln.  In addn. to the stable SEI on a hard carbon (HC) anode, we also show a stable interphase formation on a NaNi0.68Mn0.22Co0.1O2 (NaNMC) cathode.  Our HC||NaNMC full cell with this electrolyte demonstrates &gt;90% capacity retention after 300 cycles when charged to 4.2 V.  This study enables high-voltage NIBs with long cycling performance and provides a guiding principle in electrolyte design for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp6-mgtLx7nR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpge83H0c8Yw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhvVCntbbJ&amp;md5=27df3174814e23e6530bb6a56e2037b4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.13208/j.electrochem.2219012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Hao-Ran</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Which Factor Dominates Battery Performance: Metal Ion Solvation Structure-Derived Interfacial Behavior or Solid Electrolyte Interphase Layer?</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solvation structure and solid electrolyte interface engineering for excellent Na+ storage performances of hard carbon with the ether-based electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lv, Zhiqiang; Li, Tianyu; Hou, Xin; Wang, Canpei; Zhang, Huamin; Yan, Jingwang; Zheng, Qiong; Li, Xianfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">430</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">133143</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Compared with the commonly used ester-based electrolytes, more excellent Na+ storage performances can be achieved for hard carbon in the ether-based electrolyte.  Whereas, the mysteries underlying such excellent electrochem. performances are still unclear.  Herein, the impressive Na+ storage behaviors of hard carbon in the ether-based electrolyte were clarified based on a profound insight of Na+ storage mechanism.  It's revealed that the co-intercalation behavior is responsible for the lower de-solvation energy, which contributes to a facile de-solvation process and the enhanced charge transfer kinetic.  Besides, a thin, amorphous and flexible solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) in ether-based electrolyte with a specific structure where the amorphous nanoparticles are coated with org. species was probed.  And the resulted SEI is beneficial to achieving much lower activation energy for Na+ diffusion through SEI and a stable interface during cycling due to its excellent ion-conducting ability and mech. flexibility.  It's also demonstrated that ether-based solvent with short chain length plays a pos. impact on the Na+ storages, which also well agrees with the above synergistic effect.  The research plays a significant role in elucidating the uniqueness of ether-based electrolytes to hard carbon and promoting its practical application in future sodium-based battery chemistries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqavR5NQA9d1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpge83H0c8Yw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXitlGhtbvI&amp;md5=9ab1baaa976c6b6b4bc555881a1f5fc5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202100278"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Cai</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Huang</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Pan</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineering Solid Electrolyte Interface at Nano-Scale for High-Performance Hard Carbon in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2100278</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineering the structure and chem. of solid electrolyte interface (SEI) on electrode materials is crucial for rechargeable batteries.  Using hard carbon (HC) as a platform material, a correlation between Na+ storage performance, and the properties of SEI is comprehensively explored.  It is found that a "good" SEI layer on HC may not be directly assocd. with certain kinds of SEI components, such as NaF and Na2O.  Whereas, arranging nano SEI components with refined structures constructs the foundation of "good" SEI that enables fast Na+ storage and interface stability of HC in Na-ion batteries.  A layer-by-layer SEI on HC with inorg.-rich inner layer and tolerant org.-rich outer flexible layer can facilitate excellent rate and cycling life.  Besides, SEI layer as the gate for Na+ from electrolyte to HC electrode can modulate interfacial crystallog. structures of HC with pillar-solvent that function as "pseudo-SEI" for fast and stable Na+ storage in optimal 1 M NaPF6-TEGDME electrolytes.  Such a layer-by-layer SEI combined with a "pseudo-SEI" layer for HC enables an outstanding rate of 192 mAh g-1 at 2 C and stable cycling over 1100 cycles at 0.5 C.  This study provides valuable guidance to improve the electrochem. performance of electrode materials through regulation of SEI in optimal electrolytes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqaEBaB3y6f5bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpge83H0c8Yw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXptVKntrY%253D&amp;md5=995bbafbf31905c7e725155ce5fb1f6a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE03367A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Wang</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, Zhang</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Zheng</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Achieving superb sodium storage performance on carbon anodes through an ether-derived solid electrolyte interphase</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Achieving superb sodium storage performance on carbon anodes through an ether-derived solid electrolyte interphase</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jun; Wang, Da-Wei; Lv, Wei; Zhang, Siwei; Liang, Qinghua; Zheng, Dequn; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">370-376</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High sp. surface area carbon (HSSAC) is a class of promising high-capacity anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  A crit. bottleneck of the HSSAC anode, however, is the ultra-low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) in commonly used ester-based electrolytes.  This phenomenon further prohibits improving the specific capacity, long-term stability and rate capability of HSSAC anodes.  This work reports the largely enhanced anode performance of several different HSSAC anodes in ether-based electrolytes.  Very importantly, with the reduced graphene oxide (rGO) anode as one example, the ICE can be as high as 74.6% accompanied by a large reversible specific capacity of 509 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1. 75.2% of the capacity was retained after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1, the specific capacity of the rGO anode can be obtained at 196 mA h g-1.  This extraordinary performance is ascribed to the stable, thin, compact, uniform and ion conducting solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed in an ether-based electrolyte.  Fortunately, this SEI-modifying strategy is generic and is independent of the specific microstructures of HSSAC anodes, indicating a promising avenue for manipulating the SEI on HSSAC anodes through utilizing ether solvents to enable achievement of high ICE for large-capacity HSSAC anodes for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2QXpPrjk4ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpge83H0c8Yw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitV2mtbnN&amp;md5=be5958dc01f38deeacf6a2a0eb32101f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1149/2.0901802jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lucht</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Reduction Reactions of Electrolyte Salts for Lithium Ion Batteries: LiPF6,LiBF4, LiDFOB, LiBOB, and LiTFSI</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reduction Reactions of Electrolyte Salts for Lithium Ion Batteries: LiPF6, LiBF4, LiDFOB, LiBOB, and LiTFSI</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Parimalam, Bharathy S.; Lucht, Brett L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The redn. products of common Li salts for Li ion battery electrolytes, LiPF6, LiBF4, Li bisoxalato borate (LiBOB), Li difluorooxalato borate (LiDFOB), and Li trifluorosulfonylimide (LiTFSI), were studied. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">48</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2209523</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202209523</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D32%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D48%26author%3DLi%2BYi%26author%3DWang%2BZhong%26author%3DGuo%2BWang%26author%3D%2BWang%26author%3D%2BYan%26title%3DUnraveling%2Bthe%2BMechanism%2Bof%2BDifferent%2BKinetics%2BPerformance%2Bbetween%2BEther%2Band%2BCarbonate%2BEster%2BElectrolytes%2Bin%2BHard%2BCarbon%2BElectrode%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.202209523&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c19126&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.202209523&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unraveling mechanism of different kinetics performance between ether and carbonate ester electrolytes in hard carbon electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Xiaoli; Li, Xinhai; Zhong, Jing; Wang, Siwu; Wang, Zhixing; Guo, Huajun; Wang, Jiexi; Yan, Guochun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2209523</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ether electrolytes exhibit better rate kinetics than carbonate ester electrolytes when used in several kinds of anode materials, esp. in hard carbon (HC) for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the mechanism causing the remarkable kinetics difference is still unclear.  Here, a three-electrode system is used first to eliminate the influence of polarization from the Na counter electrode.  Then, there is systematic exploration from three steps of the electrode reaction process (Na+) storage in HC; de-solvation; Na+ migration through solid electrolyte interphase (SE), and the underlying mysteries are uncovered.  For Na+ storage in the bulk of the HC, it is found that two systems show the same storage mechanism and Na metallic nanoparticles will appear when discharged to 0.1 V.  In addn., faster de-solvation of the ether electrolyte is uncovered by three-electrode temp.-dependent EIS and solvation free energies calcn.  Moreover, the difference of the SEI layers is unraveled by XPS etching, SEM, and differential electrochem. mass spectrometry.  Most importantly, by discriminating the impacts of the SEI layers and de-solvation behavior, it can be concluded that the de-solvation process is the rate-controlling step of the electrode reaction process and is the main factor causing the kinetics differences between the two electrolytes.  The research provides a clear mechanism to illuminate fast kinetics for ether electrolytes, which will promote its application in SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoOORJHeYrcFrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9EebjgHt0WA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFSku7%252FI&amp;md5=06b1ce2b7c2d90d7080a31b7c6557553</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202301354"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Cao</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wahyudi, Ma</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Cavallo</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ming</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolyte-Mediated Misconception of Carbon-Based Electrode Performance and Beyond in Metal-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">29</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2301354</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202301354</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26issue%3D29%26author%3DCao%2BWang%26author%3DMa%2BWahyudi%26author%3DCavallo%2BLiang%26author%3D%2BLi%26author%3D%2BMing%26title%3DElectrolyte-Mediated%2BMisconception%2Bof%2BCarbon-Based%2BElectrode%2BPerformance%2Band%2BBeyond%2Bin%2BMetal-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202301354&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c19126&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202301354&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolyte-Mediated Misconception of Carbon-Based Electrode Performance and Beyond in Metal-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yuqi; Cao, Zhen; Wahyudi, Wandi; Ma, Zheng; Liang, Yao; Cavallo, Luigi; Li, Qian; Ming, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2301354</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A half-cell that is composed of electrode and metal (e.g., lithium) is the most classical model for examg. electrode performance in battery community, by which the voltage vs. capacity profile is the important indicator.  However, it is found that these results are not all reliable, as a misconception of electrode performance can be caused once the electrolyte is chem. unstable.  As a paradigm, it is demonstrated that the di-Et carbonate (DEC) solvent can chem. react with lithium metal to form insol. and sol. byproducts, which can accumulate on the lithium anode to influence the lithium potential and/or migrate to the counter electrode to proceed with the uncompleted electrochem. reactions.  The resultant voltage-capacity profile cannot reflect the actual electrode performance, such as the lithium storing capability within the graphite.  The reason for this phenomenon is elucidated based on solvation chem., particularly the mechanism of mitigating it by introducing ethylene carbonatesolvent to form new hydrogen bonds.  The viewpoint is further verified by employing the full cell and also extended in sodium and potassium batteries.  This study shows the necessity of discerning the reliability of electrode performance and also sheds light on the importance of designing a compatible electrolyte to examine electrode performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOS9EQJab_5bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9EebjgHt0WA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXht1GisbrN&amp;md5=0aad9a51b0d08246f06233794d234720</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/advs.202201207"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, Zou</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Wang</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Ming</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alshareef</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolyte Solvation Structure Design for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">22</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2201207</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/advs.202201207</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DAdv.%2BSci.%26issue%3D22%26author%3DZou%2BTian%26author%3DWang%2BLiu%26author%3DMing%2BYin%26author%3D%2BAlshareef%26title%3DElectrolyte%2BSolvation%2BStructure%2BDesign%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadvs.202201207&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c19126&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadvs.202201207&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolyte Solvation Structure Design for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tian, Zhengnan; Zou, Yeguo; Liu, Gang; Wang, Yizhou; Yin, Jian; Ming, Jun; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2201207</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASDCCF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  In the past two decades, exploring new electrolytes for SIBs has generally relied on the "solid electrolyte interphase (SEI)" theory to optimize the electrolyte components.  However, many obsd. phenomena cannot be fully explained by the SEI theory.  Therefore, electrolyte solvation structure and electrode-electrolyte interface behavior have recently received tremendous research interest to explain the improved performance.  Considering there is currently no review paper focusing on the solvation structure of electrolytes in SIBs, a systematic survey on SIBs is provided, in which the specific solvation structure design guidelines and their consequent impact on the electrochem. performance are elucidated.  The key driving force of solvation structure formation, and the recent advances in adjusting SIB solvation structures are discussed in detail.  It is believed that this review can provide new insights into the electrolyte optimization strategies of high-performance SIBs and even other emerging battery systems.  Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are considered the most promising battery technol. in the post-lithium era due to the abundant sodium reserves.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoTnyjkCnEzvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9EebjgHt0WA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XitFams7%252FL&amp;md5=359d2549d0ec9ed9d114024350cf020d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202300841"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Dong</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolytes with Solvating Inner Sheath Engineering for Practical Na–S Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>35</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2300841</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.202300841</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D35%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DDong%2BGuo%26title%3DElectrolytes%2Bwith%2BSolvating%2BInner%2BSheath%2BEngineering%2Bfor%2BPractical%2BNa%25E2%2580%2593S%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.202300841&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c19126&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.202300841&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolytes with Solvating Inner Sheath Engineering for Practical Na-S Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Dong; Wang, Jiaao; Lai, Tianxing; Henkelman, Graeme; Manthiram, Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">35</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2300841</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-sulfur (Na-S) batteries with durable Na-metal stability, shuttle-free cyclability, and long lifespan are promising to large-scale energy storages.  However, meeting these stringent requirements poses huge challenges with the existing electrolytes.  Herein, a localized satd. electrolyte (LSE) is proposed with 2-methyltetrahydrofuran (MeTHF) as an inner sheath solvent, which represents a new category of electrolyte for Na-S system.  Unlike the traditional high concn. electrolytes, the LSE is realized with a low salt-to-solvent ratio and low diluent-to-solvent ratio, which pushes the limit of localized high concn. electrolyte (LHCE).  The appropriate mol. structure and solvation ability of MeTHF regulate a satd. inner sheath, which features a reinforced coordination of Na+ to anions, enlarged Na+-solvent distance, and weakened anion-diluent interaction.  Such electrolyte configuration is found to be the key to build a sustainable interphase and a quasi-solid-solid sulfur redox process, making a dendrite-inhibited and shuttle-free Na-S battery possible.  With this electrolyte, pouch cells with decent cycling performance under rather demanding conditions are demonstrated.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq21zq7vaLs07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9EebjgHt0WA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXovVGmuro%253D&amp;md5=0755d55689a15387531b8098c0a5b0b2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2021.07.005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Tsolakidou</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mariyappan, Tarascon</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Trabesinger</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unraveling gas evolution in sodium batteries by online electrochemical mass spectrometry</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>42</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">12</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">21</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.ensm.2021.07.005</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D42%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D12-21%26journal%3DEnergy%2BStorage%2BMater.%26author%3DTsolakidou%2BZhang%26author%3DTarascon%2BMariyappan%26author%3D%2BTrabesinger%26title%3DUnraveling%2Bgas%2Bevolution%2Bin%2Bsodium%2Bbatteries%2Bby%2Bonline%2Belectrochemical%2Bmass%2Bspectrometry%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.ensm.2021.07.005&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c19126&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.ensm.2021.07.005&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Cycling performance of NFM//Na cells (2.0–4.2 V) at 0.2 C with 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in G4 (PG), 1 M NaBF<sub>4</sub> in G4 (BG) and 0.9 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> + 0.1 M NaBF<sub>4</sub> in G4 (PB91) electrolytes (a); first charge and discharge profiles of NFM//Na cells with three electrolytes (b); initial cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves of NFM//Na cells with a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> in three electrolytes (c), three CV curves are all from the first CV curves in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c19126/suppl_file/am3c19126_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>; cycling performance of NFM//HC full cells with three electrolytes at 0.2 C (d); Nyquist plots of NFM//Na and HC//Na cells in three electrolytes; the NFM and HC electrodes were obtained from the disassembled NFM//HC full cells after 100 cycles at 0.2 C and then the NFM and HC electrodes were reassembled with Na electrodes to distinguish the impedance of NFM and HC electrodes (e); fitting results of <i>R</i><sub>CEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values of NFM//Na cells with PG, BG, and PB91 electrolytes (f).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c19126/asset/images/large/am3c19126_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.3c19126&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig2"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c19126/asset/images/medium/am3c19126_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c19126/asset/images/large/am3c19126_0002.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr2" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Complete cycling protocol used to measure self-discharge (a); typical performance of NFM//HC full cells cycled at 0.2 C with different pause times in fully charged state, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c19126/suppl_file/am3c19126_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>; specific charge (red dots) and discharge (blue dots) capacity with PG, BG, and PB91 electrolytes (b); capacity loss ratio of NFM//HC full cells (c), capacity loss ratio = (1 – <i>C<sub>n</sub></i>/<i>C</i><sub><i>n</i>–1</sub>) × 100% (<i>n</i> is the number of pause steps, and <i>C</i> represents discharge specific capacity); chronoamperometry tests (d) to measure the current changes by holding the voltage of the NFM//HC full cells at 4.0 V with PG, BG, and PB91 electrolytes; content of transition metal elements (Ni, Fe, and Mn) deposited on the cycled HC anodes by ICP atomic emission spectrometry (e), HC electrodes were obtained from NFM//HC full cells cycled 50 times at 0.2 C.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c19126/asset/images/large/am3c19126_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.3c19126&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig3"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c19126/asset/images/medium/am3c19126_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c19126/asset/images/large/am3c19126_0003.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr3" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Characterization of the CEI layers on NFM cathodes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Exploration of alternative energy storage systems has been more than necessary in view of the supply risks haunting lithium-ion batteries.  Among various alternative electrochem. energy storage devices, sodium-ion battery outstands with advantages of cost-effectiveness and comparable energy d. with lithium-ion batteries.  Thanks to the similar electrochem. mechanism, the research and development of lithium-ion batteries have forged a solid foundation for sodium-ion battery explorations.  Advancements in sodium-ion batteries have been witnessed in terms of superior electrochem. performance and broader application scenarios.  Here, the strategies adopted to optimize the battery components (cathode, anode, electrolyte, separator, binder, current collector, etc.) and the cost, safety, and commercialization issues in sodium-ion batteries are summarized and discussed.  Based on these optimization strategies, assembly of functional (flexible, stretchable, self-healable, and self-chargeable) and integrated sodium-ion batteries (-actuators, -sensors, electrochromic, etc.) have been realized.  Despite these achievements, challenges including energy d., scalability, trade-off between energy d. and functionality, cost, etc. are to be addressed for sodium-ion battery commercialization.  This review aims at providing an overview of the up-to-date achievements in sodium-ion batteries and serves to inspire more efforts in designing upgraded sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGogiPMxi_Y61bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgQsuAomxFf8w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXpvFShsbY%253D&amp;md5=0d50fba27e49580cd9941f3f59be2404</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1039/C6CS00776G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span>. <i>Chem.
